Treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor inhibited tumour growth (Supplementary Fig. 86b). In comparison, free IL-12 mRNA and free IDO inhibitor failed to exhibit anti-tumour function relative to the PBS-treated group (Supplementary Fig. 86c). Long-term monitoring of tumour progression and mouse survival showed that while LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA partially suppressed tumour burden, they were unable to eradicate tumours (Supplementary Fig. 86d).

We next assessed systemic toxicity of the seven distinct treatment groups. Serum was collected on day 12 for assessment of cytokine levels, liver function markers and pro-inflammatory cytokines (Supplementary Fig. 87a). All LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA elevated serum levels of IL-6, TNF-慣 and IFN款 after intravenous injection (Supplementary Fig. 87b?밺), while treatment with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc LNP resulted in serum cytokine levels comparable to the negative control (Supplementary Fig. 87b?밺). Similarly, all LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA increased levels of the liver enzymes aspartate aminotransferase (AST) and alanine aminotransferase (ALT) compared with the PBS group (Supplementary Fig. 88). By contrast, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP administered via intratumoural injection did not increase serum IL-6 and TNF-慣 relative to PBS treatment (Supplementary Fig. 87e?밽), and these cytokine levels were 3.4-fold and 2.2-fold lower, respectively, than those after intravenous administration of pLNP (Supplementary Fig. 87h,i). No significant hepatotoxicity was observed after intratumoural injection of any treatment (Supplementary Fig. 89). Together, although pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA has moderate anti-tumour efficacy after intravenous injection, systemic toxicity limits the potential of the platform via systemic administration. By contrast, intratumoural injection of pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA boasts significant anti-cancer efficacy with minimal systemic toxicity.

#### **Intratumoural pLNP administration prevents rechallenge and regresses distal tumours**

Since G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs elicited a substantial memory T cell response upon intratumoural administration, we tested whether this platform could be used to protect against tumour rechallenge. To this end, we inoculated mice with subcutaneous MC38 tumours and administered G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP intratumourally at an mRNA dose of 2.5?됌펓 per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10. On day 30, MC38 cancer cells were injected into the flank of mice with primary MC38 tumours that were previously eliminated by pLNP treatment or age-matched normal mice as a control (Fig. [6a](#page-8-0)). All mice that successfully eliminated their primary tumours after G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP treatment rejected growth of a secondary tumour (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and survived to the terminal endpoint (>60 days) without detectable tumour burden (Fig. [6d\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, control mice grew tumours (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and all succumbed to their tumour burden within 40 days (Fig. [6d](#page-8-0)). No loss in body weight

or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP in only the right tumour. Tumour growth and mouse survival in each group were monitored. **g**, Representative images of tumours on day 30 after initiation of treatment. **h**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in different treatment groups. **i**, Survival curves from the four different treatment groups. **j**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **h**??*j** were *n*???? for PBS and G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP groups, *n*???? for G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP groups. **k**,**l**, Quantification of CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells (**k**) and CD4+ T cells (**l**) among CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells in contralateral tumour tissue after treatment (*n*????). Data are presented as mean?됀기뎤.d. Statistical differences in **b** were calculated using two-way ANOVA with Sidak's multiple comparisons test. ![](_page_9_Figure_2.jpeg)

was observed in the treatment group after tumour rechallenge (Fig. [6e\)](#page-8-0). Taken together, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP not only has the potential to treat and eliminate primary tumours, but can also induce sufficient immune memory to protect against local tumour regrowth.

We next probed whether the global immunomodulatory effect of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP could drive the regression of tumours distal to the primary tumour injection site. To test this, mice were inoculated with two subcutaneous MC38 tumours, one on each flank. Then, only the right tumour was injected with either PBS (negative control), G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP at an mRNA dose of 2.5?됌펓 per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Fig. [6f\)](#page-8-0). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP induced notable regression of not only the treated tumour but also the contralateral tumour (Fig. [6g,h\)](#page-8-0). All mice treated with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP survived to the terminal endpoint, nearly 3 months after tumour inoculation (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, both flank tumours of G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP-treated mice showed rapid growth and resulted in minimal survival benefit relative to PBS-treated mice, demonstrating that IDO inhibitor alone is not sufficient for therapeutic efficacy (Fig. [6h,i](#page-8-0)). For the G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP-treated mice, untreated distal tumour growth was not inhibited (Fig. [6h](#page-8-0)), limiting long-term survival without a cleavable IDO inhibitor (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). No body weight changes were observed in all treatment groups, demonstrating the biocompatibility of pLNP platforms (Fig. [6j\)](#page-8-0). Finally, we explored changes in T cell populations within the contralateral TME via flow cytometry. Akin to the perturbation of T cell populations observed within the primary tumour (Fig. [5b](#page-6-0)), treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in greater CD8+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90). Of note, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in lower numbers of CD4+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90), likely resulting in effective tumour regression owing to reduction of tumour-protective regulatory T cells. Together, these results imply that both IDO inhibitor release and IL-12 expression are necessary within pLNP for elimination of distal tumours and maximal therapeutic efficacy of this platform.

#### **Conclusion**

In this study, we engineered a synergistic immunotherapy platform, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP, which showed robust anti-tumour efficacy. Further optimization of this therapeutic platform could be accomplished by balancing pLNP stability and IDO inhibitor release. Several factors influence pLNP stability, including the tail length of pIL and the molar ratio of the helper lipids in the LN[P50,](#page-11-28) which modulate the intramolecular forces that drive pLNP formulation. The chemical structures of constituent lipids within pLNPs are likely to influence IDO release kinetics. Different linker chemistries may be designed to respond to specific biological triggers in the TME, such as pH, redox markers (for example, reactive oxygen species (ROS) and GSH) or enzymatic activity[41](#page-11-20). While in the present study we utilized a cyclic reaction for IDO inhibitor release, self-immolative linkers based on 1,6- or 1,4-azaquinone methide elimination could also be used to precisely control IDO inhibitor release kinetics[51](#page-11-29). Optimization of these parameters may identify a next-generation pLNP formulation that balances stability and IDO inhibitor release to achieve superior therapeutic outcomes.

Free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP plus free IDO inhibitor, or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP were administered either intravenous or intratumoural injection on day 6, day 8, and day 10. PBS served as negative control. The serum of mice from each treatment group was collected on day 12. (**B-G**) IL-6, TNF-慣, and IFN-款 levels in serum after intravenous or intratumoural injection of each treatment. (**H-J**) Comparison of IL-6, TNF-慣, and IFN-款 levels in serum after intravenous or intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. Data are presented as mean 짹 SD from *n=*3 biologically independent samples. Statistical differences were calculated using one-way ANOVA with Tukey's multiple comparisons test in B-G, and Student's t-tests in H-J (ns indicated no significance).

![](_page_96_Figure_0.jpeg)

**Supplementary Fig. 88**. AST and ALT levels after intravenous injection of pLNP or control therapeutics. Tumour-bearing mice were intravenously injected with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP plus free IDO inhibitor, or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. PBS was injected as a negative control. AST and ALT levels were quantified via ELISA. Data are presented as mean 짹 SD from *n=*3 biologically independent samples. Statistical differences were calculated using one-way ANOVA with Dunnett's multiple comparisons test (ns indicated no significance).

def path_from_mapping_value(paper_folder: Path, value: Any) -> Path | None:
    if not isinstance(value, str) or not value.strip():
        return None
    path = Path(value.strip())
    if not path.is_absolute():
        path = paper_folder / path
    return path


def iter_total_figure_mapping_entries(data: Any):
    if not isinstance(data, dict):
        return
    for key, value in data.items():
        if not isinstance(value, dict):
            continue
        if isinstance(key, str) and key.startswith("_"):
            continue
        if any(field in value for field in ("source_image", "source_pdf", "source_page", "panels", "caption")):
            yield value
            continue
        for item_key, entry in value.items():
            if isinstance(item_key, str) and item_key.startswith("_"):
                continue
            if isinstance(entry, dict):
                yield entry


def render_pdf_page(paper_folder: Path, source_pdf: str, source_page: int, dpi: int = 220) -> str:
    try:
        import fitz
    except ImportError as exc:
        raise RuntimeError("PyMuPDF is required for PDF page render fallback. Install package 'pymupdf'.") from exc

    if source_page < 1:
        raise ValueError(f"source_page must be a 1-based positive integer, got {source_page!r}")

    pdf_path = Path(source_pdf)
    if not pdf_path.is_absolute():
        pdf_path = paper_folder / pdf_path
    if not pdf_path.is_file():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"source_pdf does not exist: {pdf_path}")

    out_dir = paper_folder / "pdf_page_renders"
    out_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    out_path = out_dir / f"{pdf_path.stem}_page_{source_page:03d}.png"
    if out_path.exists():
        return rel_to_paper(out_path, paper_folder)

    doc = fitz.open(str(pdf_path))
    try:
        if source_page > doc.page_count:
            raise ValueError(f"source_page {source_page} exceeds page count {doc.page_count} for {pdf_path}")
        page = doc[source_page - 1]
        pix = page.get_pixmap(dpi=dpi)
        pix.save(str(out_path))
    finally:
        doc.close()
    return rel_to_paper(out_path, paper_folder)


def is_local_path_value(value: Any) -> bool:
    if not isinstance(value, str) or not value.strip():
        return False
    lowered = value.strip().lower()
    return not re.match(r"^[a-z][a-z0-9+.-]*://", lowered) and not lowered.startswith("data:")


def missing_mapping_paths(paper_folder: Path, data: Any, fields: set[str]) -> list[str]:
    missing: list[str] = []
    for entry in iter_total_figure_mapping_entries(data):
        for field in fields:
            value = entry.get(field)
            if not is_local_path_value(value):
                continue
            path = path_from_mapping_value(paper_folder, value)
            if path and not path.exists():
                missing.append(f"{field}={value}")
    return missing


def invalid_source_quality_values(data: Any) -> list[str]:
    invalid: list[str] = []
    for entry in iter_total_figure_mapping_entries(data):
        value = entry.get("source_quality")
        if value is None or value == "":
            continue
        if str(value) not in VALID_SOURCE_QUALITIES:
            invalid.append(str(value))
    return invalid


def safe_name(value: str) -> str:
    cleaned = re.sub(r"[^A-Za-z0-9_.-]+", "_", value.strip())
    return cleaned.strip("._") or "paper"


def normalize_token(value: str) -> str:
    return re.sub(r"[^a-z0-9]+", "", value.lower())


def truthy_selection(value: str) -> bool:
    return value.strip().lower() in {"yes", "maybe", "y", "true", "1", "selected"}


def row_item_id(row: dict[str, str]) -> str:
    for key in ("item_id", "pdf_item_id", "item", "label", "base_id"):
        value = (row.get(key) or "").strip()

        'selected_source_for_paneling': '',
        'manual_required': True,
        'confidence': 'unmatched',
        'reason': '',
        'panels': {},
    }
    if r.get('matched_sheet_file'):
        entry['source_table'] = (r.get('matched_sheet_file') or '').strip()
    if r.get('matched_block_csv_path'):
        entry['source_table_block'] = (r.get('matched_block_csv_path') or '').strip()
    if reason:
        entry['classification_reason'] = reason

    if base_id in main_map:
        folder, img, pdf, page = main_map[base_id]
        entry.update({
            'source_image': img,
            'source_pdf': pdf,
            'source_page': page,
            'source_quality': 'ok',
            'selected_source_for_paneling': img,
            'manual_required': False,
            'confidence': 'high',
            'reason': f'Mapped to the full {base_id} crop in QS_2026.md; caption identifies the selected panel/item and the image contains the corresponding multi-panel figure.',
        })
        if item_id == 'figure 3e':
            entry['reason'] += ' Panel e is present in the full Figure 3 crop with the microscopy quantification.'
        if item_id == 'figure 5h':
            entry['reason'] += ' Panel h is the volcano plot in the full Figure 5 crop.'
        mapping[folder][item_id] = entry
        continue

    m = re.match(r'supplementary figure\\s+(\\d+)', base_id, re.I)
    if m:
        n = int(m.group(1))
        img = supp_fig_to_image.get(n)
        if img:
            page_match = re.search(r'_page_(\\d+)_', img)
            source_page = int(page_match.group(1)) + 1 if page_match else ''
            quality = 'ok'
            confidence = 'high'
            manual_required = False
            note = f'Mapped by supplementary markdown sequence: image immediately precedes the caption for Supplementary Fig. {n} in 41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.md.'
            if n == 89:
                quality = 'suspect_crop'
                confidence = 'medium'
                manual_required = True
                note += ' The caption follows two adjacent crops on the same page; the first crop is selected as primary and manual review may be needed before paneling.'
            entry.update({
                'source_image': img,
                'source_pdf': '41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.pdf',
                'source_page': source_page,
                'source_quality': quality,
                'selected_source_for_paneling': img,
                'manual_required': manual_required,
                'confidence': confidence,
                'reason': note,
            })
            if n in {52, 53}:
                entry['reason'] += ' The requested panel is the physiochemical-properties table panel C inside the full figure image.'
            mapping['41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM'][item_id] = entry
            continue

    entry['reason'] = 'No plausible source image could be assigned from the extracted markdown/image inventory without guessing.'
    mapping.setdefault('unmatched', {})[item_id] = entry

# Remove empty top-level groups only if no selected rows landed there.
mapping = {k: v for k, v in mapping.items() if v}
out.write_text(json.dumps(mapping, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + '\\n', encoding='utf-8')
print(f'wrote {out}')
print(f'selected={len(selected)} mapped={sum(len(v) for v in mapping.values())} top_keys={list(mapping)}')
